COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 257, L.D. 424, “An Act Making Certain 9 
Appropriations and Allocations and Changing Certain Provisions of the Law Necessary to 10 
the Proper Operations of State Government”  11 
Amend the bill by striking out the title and substituting the following : 12 
'An Act Making Certain Appropriations and Allocations and Changing Certain 13 
Provisions of the Law Necessary to the Proper Operations of State Government for 14 
the Fiscal Years Ending June 30, 2023, June 30, 2024 and June 30, 2025'  15 
Amend the bill by insertin g after the title and before the enacting clause the following:  16 
'Emergency preamble.  Whereas,  acts and resolves of the Legislature do not 17 
become effective until 90 days after adjournment unless enacted as emergencies; and  18 
Whereas,  the 90 -day period may no t terminate until after the beginning of the next 19 
fiscal year; and  20 
Whereas,  certain obligations and expenses incident to the operation of state 21 
departments and institutions will become due and payable immediately; and  22 
Whereas,  in the judgment of the Legisl ature, these facts create an emergency within 23 
the meaning of the Constitution of Maine and require the following legislation as 24 
immediately necessary for the preservation of the public peace, health and safety; now, 25 
therefore,'  26 
Amend the bill by striking o ut everything after the enacting clause and inserting the 27 
following:  28 
'PART A  29 
Sec. A -1.  Appropriations and allocations.   The following appropriations and 30 
allocations are made.  31 
ADMINISTRATIVE AND FINANCIAL SERVICES, DEPARTMENT OF  32

for middle school level plans.  A middle school level plan must demonstrate to the 8 
commissioner a partnership between  a school administrative unit and a career and technical 9 
education center or career and technical education region.  10

Sec. C -5. Authorization of payments.  If the State's continued obligation for any 20 
individual component contained in those sections of this Part that set the total cost of 21 
funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 22 
contributions for that purpose exceeds the level of funding provided for that component, 23 
any unexpended balances occurring in other programs may be applied to avoid proration 24 
of payments for any individual component. Any unexpended balances from this Part may 25 
not lapse but must be carried forward f or the same purpose. 26 
Sec. C -6. Limit of State's obligation.  Those sections of this Part that set the total 37 
cost of funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 38 
contributions for that purpose may not be construed to require  the State to provide payments 39 
that exceed the appropriation of funds for general purpose aid for local schools for the fiscal 40 
year beginning July 1, 2023 and ending June 30, 2024.  41

the licensee for all or part of the actual expenses incurred by the board or its agents for 2

the administrative record.  7

board. A licensee is considered incompetent in the practice if the licensee has:  27

SUMMARY  3 
PART A  4 
This Part makes appropriations and allocations of funds for fiscal year 2023 -24 and 5 
fiscal year 2024 -25. 6 
PART B  7 
This Part makes appropriations and allocations of funds for approved reclassifications 8 
and range changes.  9 
PART C  10 
This Part establishes the total cost of education from kindergarte n to grade 12, the state 11 
contribution, the annual target state share percentage and the mill expectation for the local 12 
contribution for fiscal year 2023 -24. This Part also makes permanent a career and technical 13 
education middle school grant program.  14 
PART D 15 
This Part increases the attrition rate for the 2024 -2025 biennium from 1.6% to 5% for 16 
judicial branch and executive branch departments and agencies.  17 
PART E 18 
This Part authorizes a one -time transfer at the close of fiscal year 2022 -23 of all funds 19 
in excess  of $500,000 from total unencumbered balance forward in the Personal Services 20 
and All Other line categories in the Department of Agriculture, Conservation and Forestry, 21 
Division of Forest Protection program, General Fund account to the Capital Expenditures  22 
line category in the Department of Agriculture, Conservation and Forestry, Division of 23 
Forest Protection program, General Fund account.  24 
PART F 25 
This Part requires the transfer of $3,000,000 on or before June 30, 2024 from the 26 
unappropriated surplus of the General Fund to the Department of Agriculture, Conservation 27 
and Forestry, Maine Healthy Soils Fund  program , Other Special Revenue Funds account 28 
for funding the Maine Healthy Soils Program as outlined in the Maine Revised Statutes, 29 
Title 12, chapter 7.  30 
PART  G 31 
This Part requires the transfer of $2,000,000 on or before June 30, 2024 from the 32 
unappropriated surplus of the General Fund to the Department of Agriculture, Conservation 33 
and Forestry, Farmers Drought Relief Grant Program  Fund program , Other Special 34 
Revenue Funds account for funding the Farmers Drought Relief Grant Program as outlined 35 
in the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 7, section 220 -A. 36 
PART H  37 
This Part carries forward the remaining portion of one -time funding for the 38 
environmental closure activities at the  former Maine Military Authority site in Limestone.  39 
PART I  40 4 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 257, L.D. 424  
Page 410 - 131LR1170(02)  
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT  This Part allows  the Maine Municipal Bond Bank to issue securities for building 1 
infrastructure necessary to support new or updated equipment  to career and technical 2 
education centers and career and technical education regions and extends the date by which 3 
securities may be issued to June 30, 2025.  4 
PART J 5 
This Part continues a uthorization for each individual tax expenditure provided by 6 
statute . 7 
PART K 8 
This Part authorizes the Department of Health and Human Services to transfer available 9 
balances of appropriations between the MaineCare General Fund accounts until June 30, 10 
2025.  11 
PART L 12 
This Part authorizes the Department of Health and Human Services to adopt emergency 13 
rules to implement any provisions of this legislation over which it has specific authority 14 
that has not been addressed by some other Part of this legislation without  the necessity of 15 
demonstrating that immediate adoption is necessary to avoid a threat to public health, safety 16 
or welfare.  17 
PART M 18 
This Part requires the Department of Health and Human Services to identify savings 19 
each fiscal year from MaineCare and MaineC are-related General Fund accounts to transfer 20 
to the Departmentwide program  to offset deappropriations in that program made in this 21 
legislation . 22 
PART N 23 
This Part delays the beginning of the Fiscal Stability Program within the Department 24 
of Inland Fisheries  and Wildlife to the 2026 -2027 biennium.  25 
PART O 26 
This Part adds to  the allowed purpose s for issuing Maine Governmental Facilities 27 
Authority securities for the judicial branch to include acquiring and improving properties 28 
in Lewiston, Skowhegan and Augusta.  29 
PART P 30 
This Part amends provisions of the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 10, chapter 901 by 31 
moving the Board of Dental Practice, identified in statute as an affiliated board, into a 32 
licensure program within the Department of Professional and Financial Regulation, Office 33 
of Professional and Occupational Regulation.  This Part also amends several provisions of 34 
Title 32, chapter 143 to make consistent statutory terms as part of the organizational 35 
restructuring.  36 
PART Q 37 
This Part requires  the State Controller to transfer $ 30,894,693  to the TransCap Trust 38 
Fund established in the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 30 -A, section 6006 -G to pay tow ard 39 
the remaining debt service of the series 2015A and series 2021A bonds ; and to transfer 40
